style="white-space:nowrap">\n          \xe2\x80\xa2\xc2\xa0Summer (\n          <a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">\n           DST\n          </a>\n          )\n         </span>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Time_Zone_(North_America)" title="Central Time Zone (North America)">\n          CDT\n         </a>\n         (\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC-5" title="UTC-5">\n          UTC-5\n         </a>\n         )\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedtoprow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ZIP_code" title="ZIP code">\n          ZIP codes\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td class="adr">\n         <span class="postal-code">\n          77550-77555\n         </span>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedrow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">\n          Area code(s)\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Area_code_409" title="Area code 409">\n          409\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedtoprow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Information_Processing_Standard" title="Federal Information Processing Standard">\n          FIPS code\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         48-28068\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR2_2-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-GR2-2">\n           [2]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedrow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         <a href="/wiki/Geographic_Names_Information_System" title="Geographic Names Information System">\n          GNIS\n         </a>\n         feature ID\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         1377745\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR3_3-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-GR3-3">\n           [3]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedtoprow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         Website\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <span class="url">\n          <a class="external text" href="http://cityofgalveston.org" rel="nofollow">\n           cityofgalveston\n           <wbr/>\n           .org\n          </a>\n         </span>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Galveston\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\xa1/: \'g\' in \'guy\'">\n            \xc9\xa1\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc3\xa6/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">\n            \xc3\xa6\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">\n            l\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'v\' in \'vie\'">\n            v\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\xaa/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">\n            \xc9\xaa\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">\n            s\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">\n            t\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x99n/: \'on\' in \'button\'">\n            \xc9\x99n\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">\n        <small title="English pronunciation respelling">\n         <i>\n          <b>\n           GAL\n          </b>\n          -viss-t\xc9\x99n\n         </i>\n        </small>\n       </a>\n       ) is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="Gulf Coast of the United States">\n        coastal\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Resort_town" title="Resort town">\n        resort city\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Island" title="Galveston Island">\n        Galveston Island\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Pelican_Island_(Texas)" title="Pelican Island (Texas)">\n        Pelican Island\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">\n        U.S. state\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">\n        Texas\n       </a>\n       . The community of 209.3 square miles (542\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ), with an estimated population of 50,180 in 2015, is the\n       <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">\n        county seat\n       </a>\n       and second-largest municipality of\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_County,_Texas" title="Galveston County, Texas">\n        Galveston County\n       </a>\n       . It is within\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <a href="/wiki/Greater_Houston" title="Greater Houston">\n         Houston\xe2\x80\x93The Woodlands\xe2\x80\x93Sugar Land\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       metropolitan area.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Named after\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bernardo_de_G%C3%A1lvez_y_Madrid,_Count_of_G%C3%A1lvez" title="Bernardo de G\xc3\xa1lvez y Madrid, Count of G\xc3\xa1lvez">\n        Bernardo de G\xc3\xa1lvez y Madrid, Count of G\xc3\xa1lvez\n       </a>\n       (born in\n       <a href="/wiki/Macharaviaya" title="Macharaviaya">\n        Macharaviaya\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malaga" title="Malaga">\n        Malaga\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">\n        Spain\n       </a>\n       ), Galveston\'s first European settlements on the island were built around 1816 by French pirate\n       <a href="/wiki/Louis-Michel_Aury" title="Louis-Michel Aury">\n        Louis-Michel Aury\n       </a>\n       to help the fledgling Republic of Mexico fight Spain. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Galveston" title="Port of Galveston">\n        Port of Galveston\n       </a>\n       was established in 1825 by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congress_of_Mexico" title="Congress of Mexico">\n        Congress of Mexico\n       </a>\n       following its independence from Spain. The city was the main port for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Navy" title="Texas Navy">\n        Texas Navy\n       </a>\n       during the\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Revolution" title="Texas Revolution">\n        Texas Revolution\n       </a>\n       , and later served as the capital of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">\n        Republic of Texas\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the 19th century, Galveston became a major U.S. commercial center and one of the largest\n       <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">\n        ports\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       . It was for a time Texas\' largest city, known as the "Queen City of the Gulf". It was devastated by the\n       <a href="/wiki/1900_Galveston_hurricane" title="1900 Galveston hurricane">\n        1900 Galveston Hurricane\n       </a>\n       , whose effects included flooding and a storm surge. The natural disaster on the exposed\n       <a href="/wiki/Barrier_island" title="Barrier island">\n        barrier island\n       </a>\n       is still ranked as the deadliest in United States history, with an estimated death toll of 6,000 to 12,000 people. The city subsequently emerged during the\n       <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_the_United_States" title="Prohibition in the United States">\n        Prohibition era\n       </a>\n       as a leading tourist hub and one of the most infamous\n       <a href="/wiki/Free_State_of_Galveston" title="Free State of Galveston">\n        centers of gambling\n       </a>\n       . This era ended in the 1950s.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Much of Galveston\'s economy is centered in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">\n        tourism\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">\n        health care\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shipping" title="Shipping">\n        shipping\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">\n        financial\n       </a>\n       industries. The 84-acre (340,000\xc2\xa0m\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       )\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_Medical_Branch" title="University of Texas Medical Branch">\n        University of Texas Medical Branch\n       </a>\n       campus with an enrollment of more than 2,500 students is a major economic force of the city. Galveston is home to six\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historic_districts" title="Historic districts">\n        historic districts\n       </a>\n       containing one of the largest and historically significant collections of 19th-century buildings in the United States, with over 60 structures listed in the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">\n        National Register of Historic Places\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Galveston,_Texas" title="History of Galveston, Texas">\n        History of Galveston, Texas\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Exploration_and_19th_century_development">\n        Exploration and 19th century development\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Exploration and 19th century development">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Plan_of_the_City_of_Galveston,_Texas.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="492" data-file-width="598" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Plan_of_the_City_of_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg/220px-Plan_of_the_City_of_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Plan_of_the_City_of_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg/330px-Plan_of_the_City_of_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Plan_of_the_City_of_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg/440px-Plan_of_the_City_of_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Plan_of_the_City_of_Galveston,_Texas.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Plan of the City of Galveston, Texas (circa 1845)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_City_of_Galveston.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="433" data-file-width="599" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Map_of_City_of_Galveston.jpg/220px-Map_of_City_of_Galveston.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Map_of_City_of_Galveston.jpg/330px-Map_of_City_of_Galveston.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Map_of_City_of_Galveston.jpg/440px-Map_of_City_of_Galveston.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_City_of_Galveston.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Map of City of Galveston (circa 1904)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Galveston Island was originally inhabited by members of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karankawa" title="Karankawa">\n        Karankawa\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Akokisa" title="Akokisa">\n        Akokisa\n       </a>\n       tribes who called the island\n       <i>\n        Auia\n       </i>\n       . The Spanish explorer\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cabeza_de_Vaca" title="Cabeza de Vaca">\n        Cabeza de Vaca\n       </a>\n       and his crew were shipwrecked on the island or nearby in November 1528,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HBTO_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HBTO-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       calling it\n       <i>\n        "Isla de Malhado"\n       </i>\n       ("Isle of Bad Fate"). They began their years-long trek to a Spanish settlement in Mexico City.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McComb_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-McComb-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During his charting of the Gulf Coast in 1785, the Spanish explorer\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_de_Evia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 de Evia (page does not exist)">\n        Jos\xc3\xa9 de Evia\n       </a>\n       named the island Villa G\xc3\xa1lvez or\n       <i>\n        G\xc3\xa1lveztown\n       </i>\n       in honor of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bernardo_de_G%C3%A1lvez_y_Madrid,_Count_of_G%C3%A1lvez" title="Bernardo de G\xc3\xa1lvez y Madrid, Count of G\xc3\xa1lvez">\n        Bernardo de G\xc3\xa1lvez y Madrid, Count of G\xc3\xa1lvez\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McComb_6-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-McComb-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The island\'s first permanent European settlements were constructed around 1816 by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pirate" title="Pirate">\n        pirate\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Louis-Michel_Aury" title="Louis-Michel Aury">\n        Louis-Michel Aury\n       </a>\n       to support Mexico\'s rebellion against Spain.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HTOAURY_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HTOAURY-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1817, Aury returned from an unsuccessful raid against Spain to find Galveston occupied by the pirate\n       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Lafitte" title="Jean Lafitte">\n        Jean Lafitte\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HTOAURY_7-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HTOAURY-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Lafitte organized Galveston into a pirate "kingdom" he called "Campeche", anointing himself the island\'s "head of government."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HTOLAFITTE_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HTOLAFITTE-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Lafitte remained in Galveston until 1821, when the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">\n        United States Navy\n       </a>\n       forced him and his raiders off the island.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HTOLAFITTE_8-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HTOLAFITTE-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1825 the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congress_of_Mexico" title="Congress of Mexico">\n        Congress of Mexico\n       </a>\n       established the\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Galveston" title="Port of Galveston">\n        Port of Galveston\n       </a>\n       and in 1830 erected a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Custom_House" title="Custom House">\n        customs house\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WLDPORT_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WLDPORT-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Galveston served as the capital of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">\n        Republic of Texas\n       </a>\n       when in 1836 the\n       <a href="/wiki/Interim" title="Interim">\n        interim\n       </a>\n       president\n       <a href="/wiki/David_G._Burnet" title="David G. Burnet">\n        David G. Burnet\n       </a>\n       relocated his government there.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WLDPORT_10-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WLDPORT-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1836, the French-Canadian\n       <a href="/wiki/Michel_Branamour_Menard" title="Michel Branamour Menard">\n        Michel Branamour Menard\n       </a>\n       and several associates purchased 4,605 acres (18.64\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) of land for $50,000 to found the town that would become the modern city of Galveston.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSTORM_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISSTORM-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As Anglo-Americans migrated to the city, they brought along or purchased\n       <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">\n        enslaved\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African-Americans" title="African-Americans">\n        African-Americans\n       </a>\n       , some of whom worked domestically or on the waterfront, including on riverboats.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1839, the City of Galveston adopted a charter and was incorporated by the Congress of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">\n        Republic of Texas\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSTORM_13-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISSTORM-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HTOGAL_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HTOGAL-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The city was by then a burgeoning\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_entry" title="Port of entry">\n        port of entry\n       </a>\n       and attracted many new residents in the 1840s and later among the flood of German immigrants to Texas, including Jewish merchants.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Together with ethnic Mexican residents, these groups tended to oppose slavery, support the Union during the Civil War, and join the Republican Party after the war.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During this expansion, the city had many "firsts" in the state, with the founding of institutions and adoption of inventions: post office (1836), naval base (1836), Texas chapter of a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freemasons" title="Freemasons">\n        Masonic\n       </a>\n       order (1840); cotton compress (1842), Catholic\n       <a href="/wiki/Parochial_school" title="Parochial school">\n        parochial school\n       </a>\n       (Ursuline Academy) (1847), insurance company (1854), and gas lights (1856).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSTORM_13-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISSTORM-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barrington.2C_Carol.3B_Kearney.2C_Sydney_2006_241_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Barrington.2C_Carol.3B_Kearney.2C_Sydney_2006_241-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">\n        American Civil War\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_Army" title="Confederate States Army">\n        Confederate\n       </a>\n       forces under\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_General" title="Major General">\n        Major General\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/John_B._Magruder" title="John B. Magruder">\n        John B. Magruder\n       </a>\n       attacked and expelled occupying\n       <a href="/wiki/Union_Army" title="Union Army">\n        Union\n       </a>\n       troops from the city in January 1863 in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Galveston" title="Battle of Galveston">\n        Battle of Galveston\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HTOGBAT_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HTOGBAT-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1867 Galveston suffered a\n       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">\n        yellow fever\n       </a>\n       epidemic; 1800 people died in the city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These occurred in waterfront and river cities throughout the 19th century, as did\n       <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">\n        cholera\n       </a>\n       epidemics.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beach_hotel_galveston.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1198" data-file-width="1849" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Beach_hotel_galveston.jpg/220px-Beach_hotel_galveston.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Beach_hotel_galveston.jpg/330px-Beach_hotel_galveston.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Beach_hotel_galveston.jpg/440px-Beach_hotel_galveston.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beach_hotel_galveston.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Beach_Hotel_(Galveston)" title="Beach Hotel (Galveston)">\n          The Beach Hotel\n         </a>\n         catered to vacationers until a fire in 1898.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The city\'s progress continued through the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era" title="Reconstruction era">\n        Reconstruction era\n       </a>\n       with numerous "firsts": construction of the opera house (1870), and orphanage (1876), and installation of telephone lines (1878) and electric lights (1883).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSTORM_13-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISSTORM-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barrington.2C_Carol.3B_Kearney.2C_Sydney_2006_241_16-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Barrington.2C_Carol.3B_Kearney.2C_Sydney_2006_241-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Having attracted\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedmen" title="Freedmen">\n        freedmen\n       </a>\n       from rural areas, in 1870 the city had a black population that totaled 3,000,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       made up mostly of former slaves but also by persons who were\n       <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">\n        free men of color\n       </a>\n       and educated before the war. The "blacks" comprised nearly 25% of the city\'s population of 13,818 that year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the post-Civil-War period, leaders such as George T. Ruby and\n       <a href="/wiki/Norris_Wright_Cuney" title="Norris Wright Cuney">\n        Norris Wright Cuney\n       </a>\n       , who headed the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texas_Republican_Party" title="Texas Republican Party">\n        Texas Republican Party\n       </a>\n       and promoted\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_rights" title="Civil rights">\n        civil rights\n       </a>\n       for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedmen" title="Freedmen">\n        freedmen\n       </a>\n       , helped to dramatically improve educational and employment opportunities for blacks in Galveston and in Texas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Cuney established his own business of stevedores and a union of black dockworkers to break the white monopoly on dock jobs. Galveston was a cosmopolitan city and one of the more successful during Reconstruction; the\n       <a href="/wiki/Freedmen%27s_Bureau" title="Freedmen\'s Bureau">\n        Freedmen\'s Bureau\n       </a>\n       was headquartered here. German families sheltered teachers from the North, and hundreds of freedmen were taught to read. Its business community promoted progress, and immigrants stayed after arriving at this port of entry.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By the end of the 19th century, the city of Galveston had a population of 37,000. Its position on the natural harbor of\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Bay" title="Galveston Bay">\n        Galveston Bay\n       </a>\n       along the Gulf of Mexico made it the center of trade in Texas. It was one of the nation\'s largest cotton ports, in competition with\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">\n        New Orleans\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Throughout the 19th century, the port city of Galveston grew rapidly and the Strand was considered the region\'s primary business center. For a time, the Strand was known as the "Wall Street of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_South" title="American South">\n        South\n       </a>\n       ".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the late 1890s, the government constructed\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Crockett" title="Fort Crockett">\n        Fort Crockett\n       </a>\n       defenses and coastal artillery batteries in Galveston and along the Bolivar Roads. In February 1897, the\n       <a href="/wiki/USS_Texas_(1892)" title="USS Texas (1892)">\n        <i>\n         USS Texas\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       (nicknamed Old Hoodoo), the first commissioned\n       <a href="/wiki/Battleship" title="Battleship">\n        battleship\n       </a>\n       of the United States Navy, visited Galveston. During the festivities, the ship\'s officers were presented with a $5,000 silver service, adorned with various Texas motifs, as a gift from the state\'s citizens.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_of_1900_and_recovery">\n        Hurricane of 1900 and recovery\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Hurricane of 1900 and recovery">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galveston_Hurricane_of_1900" title="Galveston Hurricane of 1900">\n        Galveston Hurricane of 1900\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_Era_of_Galveston" title="Open Era of Galveston">\n        Open Era of Galveston\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galveston_1900_Storm_Marker.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2312" data-file-width="2112" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Galveston_1900_Storm_Marker.jpg/125px-Galveston_1900_Storm_Marker.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Galveston_1900_Storm_Marker.jpg/188px-Galveston_1900_Storm_Marker.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Galveston_1900_Storm_Marker.jpg/250px-Galveston_1900_Storm_Marker.jpg 2x" width="125"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galveston_1900_Storm_Marker.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Memorial marker along the\n         <a href="/wiki/Strand_Historic_District" title="Strand Historic District">\n          Strand Historic District\n         </a>\n         indicating a building that survived the 1900 hurricane.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On September 8, 1900, the island was struck by a devastating\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">\n        hurricane\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HTOSTORM_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HTOSTORM-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galveston_Hurricane_of_1900" title="Galveston Hurricane of 1900">\n        event\n       </a>\n       holds the record as the United States\' deadliest\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_disaster" title="Natural disaster">\n        natural disaster\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HTOSTORM_28-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HTOSTORM-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The city was devastated, and an estimated 6,000 to 8,000 people on the island were killed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HTOSTORM_28-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HTOSTORM-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Following the storm, a 10-mile (16\xc2\xa0km) long, 17 foot (5.2\xc2\xa0m) high\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Seawall" title="Galveston Seawall">\n        seawall\n       </a>\n       was built to protect the city from floods and hurricane storm surges. A team of engineers including\n       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Martyn_Robert" title="Henry Martyn Robert">\n        Henry Martyn Robert\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert%27s_Rules_of_Order" title="Robert\'s Rules of Order">\n        Robert\'s Rules of Order\n       </a>\n       ) designed the plan to raise much of the existing city to a sufficient elevation behind a seawall so that confidence in the city could be maintained.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sunset_Route,_Sea_Wall,_Galveston,_Texas.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="465" data-file-width="748" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Sunset_Route%2C_Sea_Wall%2C_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg/220px-Sunset_Route%2C_Sea_Wall%2C_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Sunset_Route%2C_Sea_Wall%2C_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg/330px-Sunset_Route%2C_Sea_Wall%2C_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Sunset_Route%2C_Sea_Wall%2C_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg/440px-Sunset_Route%2C_Sea_Wall%2C_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sunset_Route,_Sea_Wall,_Galveston,_Texas.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Sunset Route, Seawall, Galveston, Texas (postcard, c. 1907)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The city developed the city commission form of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipal_government" title="Municipal government">\n        city government\n       </a>\n       , known as the "\n       <a href="/wiki/City_commission_government" title="City commission government">\n        Galveston Plan\n       </a>\n       ", to help expedite recovery.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-texashandbook_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-texashandbook-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Despite attempts to draw investment to the city after the hurricane, Galveston never returned to its levels of national importance or prosperity. Development was also hindered by the construction of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Houston_Ship_Channel" title="Houston Ship Channel">\n        Houston Ship Channel\n       </a>\n       , which brought the\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Houston" title="Port of Houston">\n        Port of Houston\n       </a>\n       into competition with the natural harbor of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Galveston" title="Port of Galveston">\n        Port of Galveston\n       </a>\n       for sea traffic. To further her recovery, and rebuild her population, Galveston actively solicited immigration. Through the efforts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Cohen_(rabbi)" title="Henry Cohen (rabbi)">\n        Rabbi Henry Cohen\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Congregation_B%27nai_Israel_(Galveston,_Texas)" title="Congregation B\'nai Israel (Galveston, Texas)">\n        Congregation B\'nai Israel\n       </a>\n       , Galveston became the focus of an immigration plan called the\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Movement" title="Galveston Movement">\n        Galveston Movement\n       </a>\n       that, between 1907 and 1914, diverted roughly 10,000\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">\n        Eastern European\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">\n        Jewish\n       </a>\n       immigrants from the usual destinations of the crowded cities of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">\n        Northeastern United States\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tshaonline.org_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tshaonline.org-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Additionally numerous other immigrant groups, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">\n        Greeks\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">\n        Italians\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Russia" title="History of the Jews in Russia">\n        Russian Jews\n       </a>\n       , came to the city during this period.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hardwick.2C_p._13_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hardwick.2C_p._13-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This immigration trend substantially altered the ethnic makeup of the island, as well as many other areas of Texas and the western U.S.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Though the storm stalled economic development and the city of Houston developed as the region\'s principal metropolis, Galveston economic leaders recognized the need to diversify from the traditional port-related industries. In 1905\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_Lewis_Moody,_Jr." title="William Lewis Moody, Jr.">\n        William Lewis Moody, Jr.\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isaac_H._Kempner" title="Isaac H. Kempner">\n        Isaac H. Kempner\n       </a>\n       , members of two of Galveston\'s leading families founded the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_National_Insurance_Company" title="American National Insurance Company">\n        American National Insurance Company\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Two years later, Moody established the City National Bank, which would become the\n       <a href="/wiki/Moody_National_Bank" title="Moody National Bank">\n        Moody National Bank\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anico.com_35-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-anico.com-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the 1920s and 1930s, the city re-emerged as a major tourist destination.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Under the influence of\n       <a href="/wiki/Sam_Maceo" title="Sam Maceo">\n        Sam Maceo\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Maceo" title="Rosario Maceo">\n        Rosario Maceo\n       </a>\n       , the city exploited the\n       <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_the_United_States" title="Prohibition in the United States">\n        prohibition\n       </a>\n       of liquor and gambling in clubs like the\n       <a href="/wiki/Balinese_Room" title="Balinese Room">\n        Balinese Room\n       </a>\n       , which offered entertainment to wealthy Houstonians and other out-of-towners. Combined with prostitution, which had existed in the city since the Civil War, Galveston became known as the "sin city" of the Gulf.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hotgalv_38-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hotgalv-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Galvestonians accepted and supported the illegal activities, often referring to their island as the "\n       <a href="/wiki/Free_State_of_Galveston" title="Free State of Galveston">\n        Free State of Galveston\n       </a>\n       ".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The island had entered what would later become known as the "open era".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The 1930s and 1940s brought much change to the Island City. During World War II, the Galveston Municipal Airport, predecessor to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scholes_International_Airport" title="Scholes International Airport">\n        Scholes International Airport\n       </a>\n       , was re-designated a U.S.\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Corps" title="United States Army Air Corps">\n        Army Air Corps\n       </a>\n       base and named "Galveston Army Air Field". In January 1943, Galveston Army Air Field was officially activated with the\n       <a href="/wiki/46th_Test_Wing" title="46th Test Wing">\n        46th Bombardment Group\n       </a>\n       serving an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-submarine" title="Anti-submarine">\n        anti-submarine\n       </a>\n       role in the Gulf of Mexico. In 1942, William Lewis Moody, Jr., along with his wife Libbie Shearn Rice Moody, established the\n       <a href="/wiki/Moody_Foundation" title="Moody Foundation">\n        Moody Foundation\n       </a>\n       , to benefit "present and future generations of Texans." The foundation, one of the largest in the United States, would play a prominent role in Galveston during later decades, helping to fund numerous civic and health-oriented programs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_of_Texas.2C_Moody_Foundation_42-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Handbook_of_Texas.2C_Moody_Foundation-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Post\xe2\x80\x93World_War_II">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post.E2.80.93World_War_II">\n        Post\xe2\x80\x93World War II\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Post\xe2\x80\x93World War II">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The end of the war drastically reduced military investment in the island. Increasing enforcement of gambling laws and the growth of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">\n        Las Vegas, Nevada\n       </a>\n       as a competitive center of gambling and entertainment put pressure on the gaming industry on the island.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Finally in 1957, Texas\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Attorney_General" title="Attorney General">\n        Attorney General\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Will_Wilson" title="Will Wilson">\n        Will Wilson\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Ranger_Division" title="Texas Ranger Division">\n        Texas Rangers\n       </a>\n       began a massive campaign of raids which disrupted gambling and prostitution in the city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As these vice industries crashed, so did tourism, taking the rest of the Galveston economy with it.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Neither the economy nor the culture of the city was the same afterward.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TM:_Grande_Dame.2C_216_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TM:_Grande_Dame.2C_216-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galveston_(Texas).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Galveston_%28Texas%29.jpg/220px-Galveston_%28Texas%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Galveston_%28Texas%29.jpg/330px-Galveston_%28Texas%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Galveston_%28Texas%29.jpg/440px-Galveston_%28Texas%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galveston_(Texas).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Downtown Galveston as viewed from the air\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The island\'s economy began a long stagnation. Many businesses relocated off the island during this period; however, health care, insurance and financial industries continue to be strong contributors to the economy. By 1959, the city of Houston had long out-paced Galveston in population and economic growth. Beginning in 1957, the Galveston Historical Foundation began its efforts to preserve historic buildings.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The 1966 book\n       <i>\n        The Galveston That Was\n       </i>\n       helped encourage the preservation movement. Restoration efforts financed by motivated investors, notably Houston businessman\n       <a href="/wiki/George_P._Mitchell" title="George P. Mitchell">\n        George P. Mitchell\n       </a>\n       , gradually developed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Strand_Historic_District" title="Strand Historic District">\n        Strand Historic District\n       </a>\n       and reinvented other areas. A new, family-oriented tourism emerged in the city over many years.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       With the 1960s came the expansion of higher education in Galveston. Already home to the University of Texas Medical Branch, the city got a boost in 1962 with the creation of the Texas Maritime Academy, predecessor of\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University_at_Galveston" title="Texas A&amp;M University at Galveston">\n        Texas A&amp;M University at Galveston\n       </a>\n       ; and by 1967 a\n       <a href="/wiki/Community_college" title="Community college">\n        community college\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_College" title="Galveston College">\n        Galveston College\n       </a>\n       , had been established.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the 2000s, property values rose after expensive projects were completed\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and demand for second homes by the wealthy increased. It has made it difficult for middle-class workers to find affordable housing on the island.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ike" title="Hurricane Ike">\n        Hurricane Ike\n       </a>\n       made landfall on Galveston Island in the early morning of September 13, 2008 as a Category 2 hurricane with winds of 110\xc2\xa0miles per hour. Damage was extensive to buildings along the seawall.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After the storm, the island was rebuilt with investments in tourism, shipping, and continued emphasis on higher education and health care. Notably the addition of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Island_Historic_Pleasure_Pier" title="Galveston Island Historic Pleasure Pier">\n        Galveston Island Historic Pleasure Pier\n       </a>\n       and the replacement of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bascule_bridge" title="Bascule bridge">\n        bascule\n       </a>\n       -type\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drawbridge_(American_English)" title="Drawbridge (American English)">\n        drawbridge\n       </a>\n       on the railroad causeway with a\n       <a href="/wiki/Vertical-lift_bridge" title="Vertical-lift bridge">\n        vertical-lift\n       </a>\n       -type drawbridge to allow heavier freight.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Island" title="Galveston Island">\n        Galveston Island\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Bay" title="Galveston Bay">\n        Galveston Bay\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GalvestonTXFromTheISS.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="679" data-file-width="1024" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/GalvestonTXFromTheISS.jpg/220px-GalvestonTXFromTheISS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/GalvestonTXFromTheISS.jpg/330px-GalvestonTXFromTheISS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/GalvestonTXFromTheISS.jpg/440px-GalvestonTXFromTheISS.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GalvestonTXFromTheISS.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Galveston, from the\n         <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n          International Space Station\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The city of Galveston is situated on Galveston Island, a\n       <a href="/wiki/Barrier_island" title="Barrier island">\n        barrier island\n       </a>\n       off the\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">\n        Texas\n       </a>\n       Gulf coast near the mainland coast. Made up of mostly sand-sized particles and smaller amounts of finer mud sediments and larger gravel-sized sediments, the island is unstable, affected by water and weather, and can shift its boundaries through erosion.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The city is about 45 miles (72\xc2\xa0km) southeast of downtown Houston.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The island is oriented generally northeast-southwest, with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">\n        Gulf of Mexico\n       </a>\n       on the east and south, West Bay on the west, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Bay" title="Galveston Bay">\n        Galveston Bay\n       </a>\n       on the north. The island\'s main access point from the mainland is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_45" title="Interstate 45">\n        Interstate Highway 45\n       </a>\n       causeway that crosses West Bay on the island\'s northeast side.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A deepwater channel connects Galveston\'s harbor with the Gulf and the Gulf Intracoastal Waterway. According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n        United States Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       , the city has an area of 209.3 square miles (542.2\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ), of which 41.2 square miles (106.8\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) are land and 168.1 square miles (435.4\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ), or 80.31%, are water.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census_2010_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Census_2010-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The island is 50 miles (80\xc2\xa0km) southeast of\n       <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">\n        Houston\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The western portion of Galveston is referred to as the "West End". Communities in eastern Galveston include Lake Madeline, Offats Bayou, Central City, Fort Crockett, Bayou Shore, Lasker Park, Carver Park, Kempner Park, Old City/Central Business District, San Jacinto, East End, and Lindale.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of 2009 many residents of the west end use\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golf_carts" title="Golf carts">\n        golf carts\n       </a>\n       as transportation to take them to and from residential houses, the Galveston Island Country Club, and stores. In 2009, Chief of Police Charles Wiley said he believed golf carts should be prohibited outside golf courses, and West End residents campaigned against any ban on their use.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2011\n       <a href="/wiki/Rice_University" title="Rice University">\n        Rice University\n       </a>\n       released a study,\n       <i>\n        "Atlas of Sustainable Strategies for Galveston Island,"\n       </i>\n       which argued the West End of Galveston was quickly eroding and the City should reduce construction and/or population in that area. It recommended against any rebuilding of the West End in the event of damage from another hurricane.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1208px;">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="">\n        <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galveston_East_End_Panoramic.jpg" title="The city of Galveston looking southeast toward the Gulf of Mexico. Downtown Galveston and the Strand Historic District are at the far right, while East Beach and the University of Texas Medical Branch Children\'s Hospital and Shriners Children\'s Burns Hospital are to the far left.">\n          <img alt="" data-file-height="418" data-file-width="2302" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Galveston_East_End_Panoramic.jpg/1200px-Galveston_East_End_Panoramic.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Galveston_East_End_Panoramic.jpg/1800px-Galveston_East_End_Panoramic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/84/Galveston_East_End_Panoramic.jpg 2x" width="1200"/>\n         </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a href="/wiki/File:Galveston_East_End_Panoramic.jpg" title="File:Galveston East End Panoramic.jpg">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The city of Galveston looking southeast toward the Gulf of Mexico. Downtown Galveston and the\n         <a href="/wiki/Strand_Historic_District" title="Strand Historic District">\n          Strand Historic District\n         </a>\n         are at the far right, while East Beach and the\n         <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_Medical_Branch" title="University of Texas Medical Branch">\n          University of Texas Medical Branch\n         </a>\n         Children\'s Hospital and\n         <a href="/wiki/Shriners_Hospitals_for_Children" title="Shriners Hospitals for Children">\n          Shriners Children\'s Burns Hospital\n         </a>\n         are to the far left.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_districts">\n        Historic districts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Historic districts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trube_Castle,_Galveston.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="896" data-file-width="1198" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Trube_Castle%2C_Galveston.jpg/220px-Trube_Castle%2C_Galveston.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Trube_Castle%2C_Galveston.jpg/330px-Trube_Castle%2C_Galveston.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Trube_Castle%2C_Galveston.jpg/440px-Trube_Castle%2C_Galveston.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trube_Castle,_Galveston.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Galveston contains many restored Victorian homes\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Galveston is home to six historic districts with over 60 structures listed representing architectural significance in the National Register of Historic Places.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NATLREG_60-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NATLREG-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Silk Stocking National Historic District, between Broadway and\n       <a href="/wiki/Seawall_Boulevard" title="Seawall Boulevard">\n        Seawall Boulevard\n       </a>\n       and bounded by Ave. K, 23rd St., Ave. P, and 26th St., contains a collection of historic homes constructed from the Civil War through World War II.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/East_End_Historic_District_(Galveston,_Texas)" title="East End Historic District (Galveston, Texas)">\n        East End Historic District\n       </a>\n       on both sides of Broadway and Market Streets, contains 463 buildings. Other historic districts include Cedar Lawn, Denver Court and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Travis" title="Fort Travis">\n        Fort Travis\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NATLREG_60-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NATLREG-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strand_National_Historic_Landmark_District" title="Strand National Historic Landmark District">\n        Strand National Historic Landmark District\n       </a>\n       is a\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">\n        National Historic Landmark District\n       </a>\n       of mainly\n       <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">\n        Victorian era\n       </a>\n       buildings that have been adapted for use as restaurants, antique stores, historical exhibits, museums and art galleries. The area is a major\n       <a href="/wiki/Tourist_attraction" title="Tourist attraction">\n        tourist attraction\n       </a>\n       for the island city. It is the center for two very popular seasonal\n       <a href="/wiki/Festival" title="Festival">\n        festivals\n       </a>\n       . It is widely considered the island\'s shopping and entertainment center. Today, "the Strand" is generally used to refer to the five-block business district between 20th and 25th streets in downtown Galveston, near the city\'s wharf.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Oleander_City">\n        Oleander City\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Oleander City">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FirstoleanderPlantinggALV.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/FirstoleanderPlantinggALV.jpg/220px-FirstoleanderPlantinggALV.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/FirstoleanderPlantinggALV.jpg/330px-FirstoleanderPlantinggALV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/FirstoleanderPlantinggALV.jpg/440px-FirstoleanderPlantinggALV.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FirstoleanderPlantinggALV.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The first Oleander in Galveston, planted in 1841\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Since the early 20th century, Galveston has been popularly known as the \'Oleander City\'\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       because of a long history of cultivating\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nerium_oleander" title="Nerium oleander">\n        Nerium oleander\n       </a>\n       , a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical" title="Subtropical">\n        subtropical\n       </a>\n       evergreen shrub which thrives on the island.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Oleanders are a defining feature of the city; when flowering (between April and October) they add masses of color to local gardens, parks, and streets. Thousands were planted in the recovery following the Hurricane of 1900 and Galvestonians continue to treasure the plant for its\' low water needs, tolerance of heat, salt spray and sandy soils.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This makes them especially resistant to the after-effects of hurricanes and tropical storms. Galveston is reputed to have the most diverse range of Oleander cultivars in the world, numbering over 100, with many varieties developed in the city and named after prominent Galvestonians.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2005 the month of May was declared "Oleander Month" by the City of Galveston\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and there are also Oleander-themed tours of the city exploring the history of the plant on the island. Since 1967 the International Oleander Society has operated in Galveston, which promotes the cultivation of the plant, organizes an Oleander festival every spring and maintains a commemorative Oleander garden in the city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">\n        Climate\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Galveston\'s climate is classified as\n       <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">\n        humid\xc2\xa0subtropical\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Cfa\n       </i>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification#GROUP_C:_Temperate.2Fmesothermal_climates" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">\n        K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification system\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Prevailing winds from the south and southeast bring both heat from the deserts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">\n        Mexico\n       </a>\n       and moisture from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">\n        Gulf of Mexico\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Summer temperatures regularly exceed 90\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (32\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) and the area\'s humidity drives the\n       <a href="/wiki/Heat_index" title="Heat index">\n        heat index\n       </a>\n       even higher, while nighttime lows average around 80\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (27\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Winters in the area are temperate with typical January highs above 60\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (16\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) and lows near 50\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (10\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C). Snowfall is generally rare; however, 15.4\xc2\xa0in (39.1\xc2\xa0cm) of snow fell in February 1895, making the 1894\xe2\x80\x9395 winter the snowiest on record. Annual rainfall averages well over 40 inches (1,000\xc2\xa0mm) a year with some areas typically receiving over 50 inches (1,300\xc2\xa0mm).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane" title="Hurricane">\n        Hurricanes\n       </a>\n       are an ever-present threat during the summer and fall season, which puts Galveston in Coastal Windstorm Area.\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Island" title="Galveston Island">\n        Galveston Island\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolivar_Peninsula" title="Bolivar Peninsula">\n        Bolivar Peninsula\n       </a>\n       are generally at the greatest risk among the communities near the Galveston Bay. However, though the island and peninsula provide some shielding, the bay shoreline still faces significant danger from storm surge.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="14">\n         Climate data for Galveston, Texas (\n         <a href="/wiki/Scholes_International_Airport_at_Galveston" title="Scholes International Airport at Galveston">\n          Scholes Int\'l\n         </a>\n         ), 1981\xe2\x88\x922010 normals, extremes 1871\xe2\x88\x92present\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n          <a href="#cite_note-79">\n           [79]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Month\n        </th>\n        <th scope="col">\n         Jan\n        </th>\n        <th scope="col">\n         Feb\n        </th>\n        <th scope="col">\n         Mar\n        </th>\n        <th scope="col">\n         Apr\n        </th>\n        <th scope="col">\n         May\n        </th>\n        <th scope="col">\n         Jun\n        </th>\n        <th scope="col">\n         Jul\n        </th>\n        <th scope="col">\n         Aug\n        </th>\n        <th scope="col">\n         Sep\n        </th>\n        <th scope="col">\n         Oct\n        </th>\n        <th scope="col">\n         Nov\n        </th>\n        <th scope="col">\n         Dec\n        </th>\n        <th scope="col" style="border-left-width:medium">\n         Year\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr style="text-align: center;">\n        <th scope="row" style="height: 16px;">\n         Record high \xc2\xb0F (\xc2\xb0C)\n        </th>\n        <td style="background: #FF6A00;
