text-align: center;">\n         \xe2\x88\x923.1%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:center">\n         <b>\n          <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">\n           2010\n          </a>\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td style="padding-left:8px;">\n         47,743\n        </td>\n        <td style="font-size:85%">\n        </td>\n        <td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">\n         \xe2\x88\x9216.6%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:center">\n         <b>\n          Est. 2016\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td style="padding-left:8px;">\n         50,550\n        </td>\n        <td style="font-size:85%">\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USCensusEst2016_85-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-USCensusEst2016-85">\n           [85]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">\n         5.9%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="4" style="border-top:1px solid black; font-size:85%; text-align:left">\n         <center>\n          U.S. Decennial Census\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DecennialCensus_86-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-DecennialCensus-86">\n            [86]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n           <a href="#cite_note-87">\n            [87]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </center>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       As of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">\n        census\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR2_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GR2-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       of 2010, there were 47,743 people, 19,943 households, and 10,779 families residing in the city. As of the 2016\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census" title="U.S. Census">\n        U.S. Census\n       </a>\n       estimate\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , the city had a total population of 50,550.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">\n        population density\n       </a>\n       was 1,159 people per square mile (447/km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ). There were 32,368 housing units at an average density of 786 per square mile (303/km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ). The racial makeup of the city was 62.5%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" title="White (U.S. Census)">\n        White\n       </a>\n       , 19.2%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" title="African American (U.S. Census)">\n        Black\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">\n        African American\n       </a>\n       , 0.9%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">\n        Native American\n       </a>\n       , 3.2%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">\n        Asian\n       </a>\n       , &lt;0.1%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">\n        Pacific Islander\n       </a>\n       , 11.0% from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">\n        other races\n       </a>\n       , and 3.3% from two or more races. 31.3% of the population were\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanics_in_the_United_States" title="Hispanics in the United States">\n        Hispanic\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">\n        Latino\n       </a>\n       of any race. There were 19,943 households out of which 20.7% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 34.4% were\n       <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">\n        married couples\n       </a>\n       living together, 14.7% had a female householder with no husband present, and 46.0% were non-families. 36.7% of all households were made up of individuals and 10.5% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.27 and the average family size was 3.02.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the city, the population was 23.4% under the age of 13, 11.3% from 13 to 24, 29.8% from 25 to 44, 21.8% from 45 to 88, and 13.7% who were 89 years of age or older. The median age was 36 years. For every 100 females there were 93.4 males. For every 100 females age 13 and over, there were 90.4 males. The median income for a household in the city was $28,895, and the median income for a family was $35,049. Males had a median income of $30,150 versus $26,030 for females. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">\n        per capita income\n       </a>\n       for the city was $18,275. About 17.8% of families and 22.3% of the population were below the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_line" title="Poverty line">\n        poverty line\n       </a>\n       , including 32.1% of those under age 13 and 14.2% of those age 89 or over.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Port_of_Galveston">\n        Port of Galveston\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Port of Galveston">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Galveston" title="Port of Galveston">\n        Port of Galveston\n       </a>\n       , also called Galveston Wharves, began as a trading post in 1825.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Today, the port has grown to 850 acres (3.4\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) of port facilities. The port is located on the Gulf\n       <a href="/wiki/Intracoastal_Waterway" title="Intracoastal Waterway">\n        Intracoastal Waterway\n       </a>\n       , on the north side of Galveston Island, with some facilities on\n       <a href="/wiki/Pelican_Island_(Texas)" title="Pelican Island (Texas)">\n        Pelican Island\n       </a>\n       . The port has facilities to handle all types of cargo including\n       <a href="/wiki/Containerization" title="Containerization">\n        containers\n       </a>\n       , dry and liquid bulk,\n       <a href="/wiki/Break_bulk_cargo" title="Break bulk cargo">\n        breakbulk\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Roll-on/roll-off" title="Roll-on/roll-off">\n        Roll-on/roll-off\n       </a>\n       , refrigerated cargo and project cargoes.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The port also serves as a passenger cruise ship terminal for cruise ships operating in the Caribbean. The terminal was\n       <a href="/wiki/Home_port" title="Home port">\n        home port\n       </a>\n       to two\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carnival_Cruise_Lines" title="Carnival Cruise Lines">\n        Carnival Cruise Lines\n       </a>\n       vessels, the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Carnival_Conquest" title="Carnival Conquest">\n         Carnival Conquest\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       and the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Carnival_Ecstasy" title="Carnival Ecstasy">\n         Carnival Ecstasy\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . In November 2011 the company made Galveston\n       <a href="/wiki/Home_port" title="Home port">\n        home port\n       </a>\n       to its 3,960-passenger mega-ships\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Carnival_Magic" title="Carnival Magic">\n         Carnival Magic\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Carnival_Triumph" title="Carnival Triumph">\n         Carnival Triumph\n        </a>\n        ,\n       </i>\n       as well.\n       <i>\n        Carnival Magic\n       </i>\n       sails a seven-day Caribbean cruise from Galveston, and it is the largest cruise ship based at the Port year-round.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Galveston is the home port to\n       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Caribbean_International" title="Royal Caribbean International">\n        Royal Caribbean International\n       </a>\n       \'s,\n       <a href="/wiki/MS_Liberty_of_the_Seas" title="MS Liberty of the Seas">\n        MS\n        <i>\n         Liberty of the Seas\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       , which is the largest cruise ship ever based here and one of the largest ships in the world. In September 2012\n       <a href="/wiki/Disney_Cruise_Line" title="Disney Cruise Line">\n        Disney Cruise Line\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Disney_Magic" title="Disney Magic">\n         Disney Magic\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       also became based in Galveston, offering four-, six-, seven-, and eight-day cruises to the Caribbean and the Bahamas.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Finance">\n        Finance\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Finance">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moody_Plaza_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="401" data-file-width="289" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Moody_Plaza_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg/170px-Moody_Plaza_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Moody_Plaza_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg/255px-Moody_Plaza_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8d/Moody_Plaza_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moody_Plaza_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/One_Moody_Plaza" title="One Moody Plaza">\n          One Moody Plaza\n         </a>\n         , the location of the\n         <a href="/wiki/American_National_Insurance_Company" title="American National Insurance Company">\n          American National Insurance Company\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/American_National_Insurance_Company" title="American National Insurance Company">\n        American National Insurance Company\n       </a>\n       , one of the largest life insurance companies in the United States, is based in Galveston. The company and its subsidiaries operate in all 50 U.S. states, the District of Columbia,\n       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">\n        Puerto Rico\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">\n        American Samoa\n       </a>\n       . Through its subsidiary, American National de M\xc3\xa9xico, Compa\xc3\xb1\xc3\xada de Seguros de Vida, it provides products and services in\n       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">\n        Mexico\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Moody_National_Bank" title="Moody National Bank">\n        Moody National Bank\n       </a>\n       , with headquarters in downtown Galveston, is one of the largest privately owned Texas-based banks. Its trust department, established in 1927, administers over 12 billion dollars in assets, one of the largest in the state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition, the regional headquarters of Iowa-based United Fire &amp; Casualty Company are located in the city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n        <a href="#cite_note-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">\n        Tourism\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Tourism">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MoodyGardens.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1232" data-file-width="2535" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/MoodyGardens.jpg/220px-MoodyGardens.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/MoodyGardens.jpg/330px-MoodyGardens.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/MoodyGardens.jpg/440px-MoodyGardens.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MoodyGardens.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Rainforest Pyramid at\n         <a href="/wiki/Moody_Gardens" title="Moody Gardens">\n          Moody Gardens\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the late 1800s Galveston was known as the "Playground of the South"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Today, it still retains a shared claim to the title among major cities along the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="Gulf Coast of the United States">\n        Gulf Coast states\n       </a>\n       . Galveston is a popular tourist destination which in 2007 brought $808 million to the local economy and attracted 5.4 million visitors. The city features an array of lodging options, including hotels such as the historic\n       <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Galvez" title="Hotel Galvez">\n        Hotel Galvez\n       </a>\n       and Tremont House, vintage bed and breakfast inns, beachfront condominiums, and resort rentals. The city\'s tourist attractions include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Island_Historic_Pleasure_Pier" title="Galveston Island Historic Pleasure Pier">\n        Galveston Island Historic Pleasure Pier\n       </a>\n       , Galveston\n       <a href="/wiki/Schlitterbahn" title="Schlitterbahn">\n        Schlitterbahn\n       </a>\n       waterpark,\n       <a href="/wiki/Moody_Gardens" title="Moody Gardens">\n        Moody Gardens\n       </a>\n       botanical park, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Star_Offshore_Drilling_Rig_%26_Museum" title="Ocean Star Offshore Drilling Rig &amp; Museum">\n        Ocean Star Offshore Drilling Rig &amp; Museum\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lone_Star_Flight_Museum" title="Lone Star Flight Museum">\n        Lone Star Flight Museum\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Railroad_Museum" title="Galveston Railroad Museum">\n        Galveston Railroad Museum\n       </a>\n       , a downtown neighborhood of historic buildings known as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strand_National_Historic_Landmark_District" title="Strand National Historic Landmark District">\n        The Strand\n       </a>\n       , many historical museums and mansions, and miles of beach front from the East End\'s Porretto Beach, Stewart Beach to the West End pocket parks.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Strand plays host to a yearly\n       <a href="/wiki/Mardi_Gras" title="Mardi Gras">\n        Mardi Gras\n       </a>\n       festival, Galveston Island Jazz &amp; Blues Festival and a Victorian-themed\n       <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">\n        Christmas\n       </a>\n       festival called\n       <a href="/wiki/Dickens_on_the_Strand" title="Dickens on the Strand">\n        Dickens on the Strand\n       </a>\n       (honoring the works of novelist\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">\n        Charles Dickens\n       </a>\n       , especially\n       <i>\n        A Christmas Carol\n       </i>\n       ) in early December. Galveston is home to several historic ships: the tall ship\n       <a href="/wiki/Elissa_(ship)" title="Elissa (ship)">\n        <i>\n         Elissa\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       (the official Tall Ship of Texas) at the Texas Seaport Museum and\n       <a href="/wiki/USS_Cavalla_(SS-244)" title="USS Cavalla (SS-244)">\n        USS\n        <i>\n         Cavalla\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/USS_Stewart_(DE-238)" title="USS Stewart (DE-238)">\n        USS Stewart\n       </a>\n       , both berthed at\n       <a href="/wiki/Seawolf_Park" title="Seawolf Park">\n        Seawolf Park\n       </a>\n       on nearby Pelican Island. Galveston is ranked the number one cruise port on the Gulf Coast and fourth in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">\n        <a href="#cite_note-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_culture">\n        Arts and culture\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Arts and culture">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Galveston_Arts_Center">\n        Galveston Arts Center\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Galveston Arts Center">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Incorporated in 1986, Galveston Arts Center (GAC) is a non-profit, non-collecting arts organization. The center exhibits contemporary art, often by Texas-based artists, and offers educational and outreach programs. Notably, GAC organizes and produces Galveston ArtWalk. Museum entry is free to the public, although cash donations are welcomed. Tiered membership options and a range of volunteer opportunities are also available.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">\n        <a href="#cite_note-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In October 2015, Galveston Arts Center will celebrate relocation to its original home, the historic 1878 First National Bank Building on the Strand. This Italianate-style 1900 Storm survivor was extensively damaged during Hurricane Ike in 2008. Fortunately, just weeks before Ike made landfall, scaffolding was installed to support the entire structural load of the building for repairs, likely preventing collapse under heavy winds and storm surge. After a lengthy fundraising campaign, restoration is nearing completion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">\n        <a href="#cite_note-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Galveston_ArtWalk">\n        Galveston ArtWalk\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Galveston ArtWalk">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       ArtWalk takes place approximately every six weeks on Saturday evenings throughout the year. ArtWalk is organized by Galveston Arts Center, which releases an ArtWalk brochure featuring a map of participating venues as well as descriptions of shows and exhibits. Venues include GAC, Galveston Artist Residency and artist\xe2\x80\x99s studios and galleries. Additionally, art is shown in \xe2\x80\x9cother walls\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94for example MOD Coffeehouse or Mosquito Cafe\xe2\x80\x94or outdoors at Art Market on Market Street. Musicians perform outdoors and at venues such as the Proletariat Gallery &amp; Public House or Old Quarter Acoustic Cafe. While most ArtWalk events are concentrated downtown, there are a number or participants elsewhere on the island.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">\n        <a href="#cite_note-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_Performing_Arts">\n        Music and Performing Arts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Music and Performing Arts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Galveston_Symphony_Orchestra">\n        Galveston Symphony Orchestra\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Galveston Symphony Orchestra">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Galveston is home to the Galveston Symphony Orchestra, an ensemble of amateur and professional musicians formed in 1979 under the direction of Richard W. Pickar, Musical Director-Conductor.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">\n        <a href="#cite_note-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Galveston_Ballet">\n        Galveston Ballet\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Galveston Ballet">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The Galveston Ballet is a regional pre-professional ballet company and academy serving Galveston county.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n        <a href="#cite_note-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The company presents one full-length classical ballet in the spring of each year and one mixed repertory program in the fall, both presented at the Grand 1894 Opera House.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Artist_Residency_&amp;_Artist_Housing">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Artist_Residency_.26_Artist_Housing">\n        Artist Residency &amp; Artist Housing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Artist Residency &amp; Artist Housing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Galveston_Artist_Residency">\n        Galveston Artist Residency\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Galveston Artist Residency">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Galveston Artist Residency (GAR) grants studio space, living space and a stipend to three visual artists each year. Resident artists work in a variety of mediums and exhibit their work in the GAR Gallery and Courtyards. Located in renovated industrial structures on the west side of downtown, GAR also hosts performances and other public events.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">\n        <a href="#cite_note-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_National_Hotel_Artist_Lofts">\n        The National Hotel Artist Lofts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: The National Hotel Artist Lofts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The National Hotel Artist Lofts (NHAL) is an Artspace-developed property featuring twenty-seven live/work units designated as affordable housing for artists.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n        <a href="#cite_note-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The project brought new life to the historic E.S. Levy Building, which was left abandoned for twenty years. Originally built as the Tremont Opera House in 1870, the structure was extensively renovated to serve various functions, from offices and stores to the National Hotel. The building also housed the U.S. National Weather Bureau\'s Galveston office under Isaac Cline during the 1900 Storm.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">\n        <a href="#cite_note-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Under Property Manager/Creative Director Becky Major, the unused retail space in the front of the building found a new purpose as a DIY art and music venue, despite its gutted and undeveloped state. In May 2015, the newly renovated space reopened as the Proletariat Gallery &amp; Public House. This bar and gallery provides a common area for NHAL and neighborhood residents and a cultural hub for the broader community. Visual art, events and live music are regularly hosted in the space.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">\n        Architecture\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Architecture">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GalvezHotelGalveston.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="794" data-file-width="1200" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/GalvezHotelGalveston.jpg/220px-GalvezHotelGalveston.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/GalvezHotelGalveston.jpg/330px-GalvezHotelGalveston.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/GalvezHotelGalveston.jpg/440px-GalvezHotelGalveston.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GalvezHotelGalveston.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galvez_Hotel" title="Galvez Hotel">\n          Galvez Hotel\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ashton_Villa_Galveston_Texas.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="440" data-file-width="500" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ashton_Villa_Galveston_Texas.jpg/220px-Ashton_Villa_Galveston_Texas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ashton_Villa_Galveston_Texas.jpg/330px-Ashton_Villa_Galveston_Texas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ashton_Villa_Galveston_Texas.jpg/440px-Ashton_Villa_Galveston_Texas.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ashton_Villa_Galveston_Texas.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Ashton Villa\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Galveston contains a large and historically significant collection of 19th-century buildings in the United States. Galveston\'s architectural preservation and revitalization efforts over several decades have earned national recognition.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">\n        <a href="#cite_note-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">\n        <a href="#cite_note-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Located in the Strand District, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_1894_Opera_House" title="Grand 1894 Opera House">\n        Grand 1894 Opera House\n       </a>\n       is a restored historic\n       <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_Revival_architecture" title="Romanesque Revival architecture">\n        Romanesque Revival\n       </a>\n       style Opera House that is currently operated as a not-for-profit\n       <a href="/wiki/Performing_arts" title="Performing arts">\n        performing arts\n       </a>\n       theater.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">\n        <a href="#cite_note-109">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Bishop%27s_Palace,_Galveston" title="Bishop\'s Palace, Galveston">\n        Bishop\'s Palace\n       </a>\n       , also known as Gresham\'s Castle, is an ornate Victorian house located on Broadway and 14th Street in the East End Historic District of Galveston, Texas. The\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Institute_of_Architects" title="American Institute of Architects">\n        American Institute of Architects\n       </a>\n       listed Bishop\'s Palace as one of the 100 most significant buildings in the United States, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">\n        Library of Congress\n       </a>\n       has classified it as one of the fourteen most representative Victorian structures in the nation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">\n        <a href="#cite_note-110">\n         [110]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galvez_Hotel" title="Galvez Hotel">\n        Galvez Hotel\n       </a>\n       is a historic hotel that opened in 1911.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carmack_111-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-carmack-111">\n         [111]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The building was named the Galvez, honoring\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bernardo_de_G%C3%A1lvez_y_Madrid,_Count_of_G%C3%A1lvez" title="Bernardo de G\xc3\xa1lvez y Madrid, Count of G\xc3\xa1lvez">\n        Bernardo de G\xc3\xa1lvez y Madrid, Count of G\xc3\xa1lvez\n       </a>\n       , for whom the city was named. The hotel was added to the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">\n        National Register of Historic Places\n       </a>\n       on April 4, 1979. The Michel B. Menard House, built in 1838 and oldest in Galveston, is designed in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_revival" title="Greek revival">\n        Greek revival\n       </a>\n       style. In 1880, the house was bought by Edwin N. Ketchum who was police chief of the city during the 1900 Storm. The Ketchum family owned the home until the 1970s. The red-brick\n       <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">\n        Victorian\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Italianate_architecture" title="Italianate architecture">\n        Italianate\n       </a>\n       home,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ashton_Villa" title="Ashton Villa">\n        Ashton Villa\n       </a>\n       , was constructed in 1859 by James Moreau Brown. One of the first brick structures in Texas, it is listed on the National Register of Historic Places and is a recorded Texas Historic Landmark. The structure is also the site of what was to become the holiday known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Juneteenth" title="Juneteenth">\n        Juneteenth\n       </a>\n       , where on June 19, 1865,\n       <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">\n        Union\n       </a>\n       General Gordon Granger, standing on its balcony, read the contents of "General Order No. 3", thereby emancipating all slaves in the state of\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">\n        Texas\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">\n        <a href="#cite_note-112">\n         [112]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handbook_113-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-handbook-113">\n         [113]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPS_114-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NPS-114">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       St. Joseph\'s Church was built by German immigrants in 1859\xe2\x80\x9360 and is the oldest wooden church building in Galveston and the oldest\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Catholics" title="German Catholics">\n        German Catholic\n       </a>\n       Church in Texas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">\n        <a href="#cite_note-115">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The church was dedicated in April 1860, to St. Joseph, the patron saint of laborers. The building is a wooden\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gothic_revival" title="Gothic revival">\n        gothic revival\n       </a>\n       structure, rectangular with a square bell tower with\n       <a href="/wiki/Trefoil" title="Trefoil">\n        trefoil\n       </a>\n       window. The U.S. Custom House began construction in 1860 and was completed in 1861. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Confederate_Army" title="Confederate Army">\n        Confederate Army\n       </a>\n       occupied the building during the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">\n        American Civil War\n       </a>\n       , In 1865, the Custom House was the site of the ceremony officially ending the Civil War.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n        <a href="#cite_note-116">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">\n        <a href="#cite_note-117">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Galveston\'s modern architecture include the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_National_Insurance_Company" title="American National Insurance Company">\n        American National Insurance Company\n       </a>\n       Tower (\n       <a href="/wiki/One_Moody_Plaza" title="One Moody Plaza">\n        One Moody Plaza\n       </a>\n       ), San Luis Resort South and North Towers, The Breakers Condominiums, The Galvestonian Resort and Condos, One Shearn Moody Plaza, US National Bank Building, the Rainforest Pyramid at Moody Gardens,\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Sealy_Hospital" title="John Sealy Hospital">\n        John Sealy Hospital\n       </a>\n       Towers at UTMB and Medical Arts Building (also known as Two Moody Plaza).\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sculpture">\n        Sculpture\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sculpture">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/%22Dignified_Resignation%22_-_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg/170px-%22Dignified_Resignation%22_-_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/%22Dignified_Resignation%22_-_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg/255px-%22Dignified_Resignation%22_-_Galveston%2C_Texas.jpg 1.5x,     <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%22Dignified_Resignation%22_-_Galveston,_Texas.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Dignified Resignation\n         </i>\n         by\n         <a href="/wiki/Louis_Amateis" title="Louis Amateis">\n          Louis Amateis\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Notable statues and sculptures in Galveston include:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         1900 Storm Memorial\n        </i>\n        , by David W. Moore\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         Birth\n        </i>\n        , by Arthur Williams\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         Dignified Resignation\n        </i>\n        by\n        <a href="/wiki/Louis_Amateis" title="Louis Amateis">\n         Louis Amateis\n        </a>\n        at the Galveston County Courthouse. With his back turned to the US flag while carrying a\n        <a href="/wiki/Flags_of_the_Confederate_States_of_America" title="Flags of the Confederate States of America">\n         Confederate flag\n        </a>\n        , it is the only memorial in Texas to feature a Confederate sailor.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n         <a href="#cite_note-118">\n          [118]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         Dolphins\n        </i>\n        by David W. Moore\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         High Tide\n        </i>\n        , by\n        <a href="/wiki/Charles_Parks" title="Charles Parks">\n         Charles Parks\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         Jack Johnson\n        </i>\n        , by Adrienne Isom\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Pink_Dolphin_Monument" title="Pink Dolphin Monument">\n         Pink Dolphin Monument\n        </a>\n        , by Joe Joe Orangias\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Texas_Heroes_Monument" title="Texas Heroes Monument">\n         Texas Heroes Monument\n        </a>\n        , by\n        <a href="/wiki/Louis_Amateis" title="Louis Amateis">\n         Louis Amateis\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">\n        Government\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Government">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GalvestonCityHall.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/GalvestonCityHall.JPG/220px-GalvestonCityHall.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/GalvestonCityHall.JPG/330px-GalvestonCityHall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/GalvestonCityHall.JPG/440px-GalvestonCityHall.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GalvestonCityHall.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Galveston City Hall\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="City_government">\n        City government\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: City government">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       After the hurricane of 1900, the city originated the City Commission form of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipal_government" title="Municipal government">\n        city government\n       </a>\n       (which became known as the "\n       <a href="/wiki/City_commission_government" title="City commission government">\n        Galveston Plan\n       </a>\n       "). The city has since adopted the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council-Manager_government" title="Council-Manager government">\n        council-manager\n       </a>\n       form of government. Galveston\'s city council serves as the city\'s legislative branch, while the city manager works as the chief executive officer, and the municipal court system serves as the city\'s judicial branch. The city council and mayor promote ordinances to establish municipal policies. The Galveston City Council consists of six elected positions, each derived from a specified\n       <a href="/wiki/Electoral_district" title="Electoral district">\n        electoral district\n       </a>\n       . Each city council member is elected to a two-year term, while the mayor is elected to a two-year term. The city council appoints the city manager, the city secretary, the city auditor, the city attorney, and the municipal judge. The city\'s Tax Collector is determined by the city council and is outsourced to Galveston County. The city manager hires employees, promotes development, presents and administers the budget, and implements city council policies.\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Joe_Jaworski&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Joe Jaworski (page does not exist)">\n        Joe Jaworski\n       </a>\n       is mayor, having replaced term-limited\n       <a href="/wiki/Lyda_Ann_Thomas" title="Lyda Ann Thomas">\n        Lyda Ann Thomas\n       </a>\n       May 2010. Jaworski is also the grandson of\n       <a href="/wiki/Leon_Jaworski" title="Leon Jaworski">\n        Leon Jaworski\n       </a>\n       , United States\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Prosecutor" title="Special Prosecutor">\n        Special Prosecutor\n       </a>\n       during the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watergate_Scandal" title="Watergate Scandal">\n        Watergate Scandal\n       </a>\n       in the 1970s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MAYOR10_119-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MAYOR10-119">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="County,_state,_and_federal_government">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="County.2C_state.2C_and_federal_government">\n        County, state, and federal government\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: County, state, and federal government">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galveston_County_Justice_Center.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1450" data-file-width="3752" height="85"        <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galveston_County_Justice_Center.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Galveston County Justice Center\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image"        <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galveston_Federal_Building_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Galveston US Post Office, Custom House and Courthouse\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Galveston is the\n       <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">\n        seat\n       </a>\n       and second-largest city (after\n       <a href="/wiki/League_City,_Texas" title="League City, Texas">\n        League City, Texas\n       </a>\n       ) of\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_County,_Texas" title="Galveston County, Texas">\n        Galveston County\n       </a>\n       in population.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">\n        <a href="#cite_note-120">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Galveston County Justice Center, which houses all the county\'s judicial functions as well as jail, is located on 59th street. The Galveston County Administrative Courthouse, the seat of civil and administrative functions, is located near the city\'s downtown.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">\n        <a href="#cite_note-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Galveston is within the County Precinct 1; as of 2008\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Patrick Doyle serves as the Commissioner of Precinct 1.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">\n        <a href="#cite_note-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Galveston County Sheriff\'s Office operates its law enforcement headquarters and jail from the Justice Center.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">\n        <a href="#cite_note-123">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">\n        <a href="#cite_note-124">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Galveston County Department of Parks and Senior Services operates the Galveston Community Center.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Galveston is located in District 23 of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_House_of_Representatives" title="Texas House of Representatives">\n        Texas House of Representatives\n       </a>\n       . As of 2008\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Craig_Eiland" title="Craig Eiland">\n        Craig Eiland\n       </a>\n       represents the district.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">\n        <a href="#cite_note-126">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Most of Galveston is within\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Senate,_District_17" title="Texas Senate, District 17">\n        District 17\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Senate" title="Texas Senate">\n        Texas Senate\n       </a>\n       ; as of 2008\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Joan_Huffman" title="Joan Huffman">\n        Joan Huffman\n       </a>\n       represents the district.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">\n        <a href="#cite_note-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A portion of Galveston is within\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Senate,_District_11" title="Texas Senate, District 11">\n        District 11\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Senate" title="Texas Senate">\n        Texas Senate\n       </a>\n       ; as of 2008\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mike_Jackson_(Texas_politician)" title="Mike Jackson (Texas politician)">\n        Mike Jackson\n       </a>\n       represents the district.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">\n        <a href="#cite_note-128">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Galveston is in\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas%27s_14th_congressional_district" title="Texas\'s 14th congressional district">\n        Texas\'s 14th congressional district\n       </a>\n       and is represented by\n       <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">\n        Republican\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Randy_Weber" title="Randy Weber">\n        Randy Weber\n       </a>\n       as of 2012\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">\n        Education\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Education">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Galveston,_Texas" title="Education in Galveston, Texas">\n        Education in Galveston, Texas\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">\n        Colleges and universities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Established in 1891 with one building and fewer than 50 students, today the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_Medical_Branch" title="University of Texas Medical Branch">\n        University of Texas Medical Branch\n       </a>\n       (UTMB) campus has grown to more than 70 buildings and an enrollment of more than 2,500 students.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">\n        <a href="#cite_note-129">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The 84-acre (340,000\xc2\xa0m\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) campus includes schools of\n       <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">\n        medicine\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nursing" title="Nursing">\n        nursing\n       </a>\n       , allied health professions, and a\n       <a href="/wiki/Graduate_school" title="Graduate school">\n        graduate school\n       </a>\n       of biomedical sciences, as well as three institutes for advanced studies &amp; medical humanities, a major medical library, seven hospitals, a network of clinics that provide a full range of primary and specialized medical care, and numerous research facilities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">\n        <a href="#cite_note-130">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Galveston is home to two post-secondary institutions offering traditional degrees in higher education.\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_College" title="Galveston College">\n        Galveston College\n       </a>\n       , a junior college that opened in 1967, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University_at_Galveston" title="Texas A&amp;M University at Galveston">\n        Texas A&amp;M University at Galveston\n       </a>\n       , an ocean-oriented branch campus of\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University" title="Texas A&amp;M University">\n        Texas A&amp;M University\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">\n        <a href="#cite_note-131">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_schools">\n        Primary and secondary schools\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary schools">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The city of Galveston is served by\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Independent_School_District" title="Galveston Independent School District">\n        Galveston Independent School District\n       </a>\n       , which includes six elementary schools, two\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Middle_School_(Galveston,_Texas)" title="Central Middle School (Galveston, Texas)">\n        middle schools\n       </a>\n       and one high school,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ball_High_School" title="Ball High School">\n        Ball High School\n       </a>\n       . There is also one\n       <a href="/wiki/Magnet_school" title="Magnet school">\n        magnet middle school\n       </a>\n       , Austin Middle School, serving grades 5 through 8.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">\n        <a href="#cite_note-132">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Galveston has several state-funded\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charter_School" title="Charter School">\n        charter schools\n       </a>\n       not affiliated with local school districts, including kindergarten through 8th grade Ambassadors Preparatory Academy and pre-kindergarten through 8th Grade Odyssey Academy.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRVSCHOOLS_133-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PRVSCHOOLS-133">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KIPP:_the_Knowledge_Is_Power_Program" title="KIPP: the Knowledge Is Power Program">\n        KIPP: the Knowledge Is Power Program\n       </a>\n       opened KIPP Coastal Village in Galveston under the auspices of GISD.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">\n        <a href="#cite_note-134">\n         [134]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Several private schools exist in Galveston. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Galveston-Houston" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Galveston-Houston">\n        Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Galveston-Houston\n       </a>\n       operates two Roman Catholic private schools, including Holy Family Catholic School (K through 8th)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">\n        <a href="#cite_note-135">\n         [135]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/O%27Connell_College_Preparatory_School" title="O\'Connell College Preparatory School">\n        O\'Connell College Preparatory School\n       </a>\n       (9-12).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRVSCHOOLS_133-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PRVSCHOOLS-133">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Other private schools include Satori Elementary School, Trinity Episcopal School, Seaside Christian Academy, and Heritage Christian Academy.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRVSCHOOLS_133-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PRVSCHOOLS-133">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n       <li      <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           <a href="/wiki/Galveston_College" title="Galveston College">\n            Galveston College\n           </a>\n          </p>\n  <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BHSGalvEntrance.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="1727" data-file-width="2358" height="88" </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:61.5px
