    </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Central Middle School, formerly\n           <a href="/wiki/Central_High_School_(Galveston,_Texas)" title="Central High School (Galveston, Texas)">\n            Central High School\n           </a>\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">\n        Media\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Media">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Daily_News_building_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1760" data-file-width="2778" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/The_Daily_News_building_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg/220px-The_Daily_News_building_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/The_Daily_News_building_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg/330px-The_Daily_News_building_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/The_Daily_News_building_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg/440px-The_Daily_News_building_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Daily_News_building_in_Galveston_Texas.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The headquarters of\n         <i>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Galveston_County_Daily_News" title="The Galveston County Daily News">\n           The Galveston County Daily News\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galveston_County_Daily_News" title="Galveston County Daily News">\n         Galveston County Daily News\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , founded in 1842, is the city\'s primary newspaper and the oldest continuously printed newspaper in Texas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">\n        <a href="#cite_note-136">\n         [136]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It currently serves as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Newspaper_of_record" title="Newspaper of record">\n        newspaper of record\n       </a>\n       for the city and the Texas City Post serves as the newspaper of record for the County. Radio station\n       <a href="/wiki/KGBC" title="KGBC">\n        KGBC\n       </a>\n       , on air from 1947\xe2\x80\x932010, has previously served as a local media outlet.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">\n        <a href="#cite_note-137">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Television station\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KHOU-TV" title="KHOU-TV">\n        KHOU\n       </a>\n       signed on the air as KGUL-TV on March 23, 1953. Originally licensed in Galveston, KGUL was the second television station to launch in the Houston area after\n       <a href="/wiki/KPRC-TV" title="KPRC-TV">\n        KPRC-TV\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KHOU_138-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KHOU-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One of the original investors in the station was actor\n       <a href="/wiki/James_Stewart" title="James Stewart">\n        James Stewart\n       </a>\n       , along with a small group of other Galveston investors.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KHOU_138-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KHOU-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In June 1959, KGUL changed its\n       <a href="/wiki/Call_sign" title="Call sign">\n        call sign\n       </a>\n       to KHOU and moved their main office to Houston. The local\n       <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" title="Hip hop">\n        hip hop\n       </a>\n       name for Galveston is "G-town."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">\n        <a href="#cite_note-139">\n         [139]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">\n        Infrastructure\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">\n        Healthcare\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Healthcare">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Galveston is the home of several of the largest\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teaching_hospitals" title="Teaching hospitals">\n        teaching hospitals\n       </a>\n       in the state, located on the campus of the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_Medical_Branch" title="University of Texas Medical Branch">\n        University of Texas Medical Branch\n       </a>\n       at Galveston. Prior to Hurricane Ike, the University employed more than 12,000 people. Its significant growth in the 1970s and 1980s was attributable to a uniquely qualified management and medical faculty including: Mr. John Thompson; Dr. William James McGanity, Dr. William Levin, Dr. David Daeschner and many more.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ike severely damaged the 550-bed\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Sealy_Hospital" title="John Sealy Hospital">\n        John Sealy Hospital\n       </a>\n       causing the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_System" title="University of Texas System">\n        University of Texas System\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Board_of_Regents" title="Board of Regents">\n        Board of Regents\n       </a>\n       to cut nearly one-third of the hospital staff. Since the storm, the regents have committed to spending $713 million to restore the campus, construct new medical towers, and return John Sealy Hospital to its 550-bed pre-storm capacity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UTMB_coming_back_stronger_than_ever_140-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-UTMB_coming_back_stronger_than_ever-140">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2011, the UT Board of Regents approved the construction of a new 13 story hospital that will be located next to John Sealy Hospital. Construction will begin in the fall of 2011, with the demolition of the old Jennie Sealy and Shriners hospitals, and continue until completion in 2016. The facility will have 250 room, 20 operating suites and 54 intensive care beds. When the new hospital is complete, along with the renovations at John Sealy, both complexes will have around 600 beds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UTMB_gets_OK_to_build_new_island_hospital_141-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-UTMB_gets_OK_to_build_new_island_hospital-141">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The university reopened their\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Level_I_Trauma_Center" title="Level I Trauma Center">\n        Level I Trauma Center\n       </a>\n       on August 1, 2009 which had been closed for eleven months after the hurricane and, as of September 2009\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , had reopened 370 hospital beds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UTMB_coming_back_stronger_than_ever_140-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-UTMB_coming_back_stronger_than_ever-140">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">\n        <a href="#cite_note-142">\n         [142]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The city is also home to a 30-bed\n       <a href="/wiki/Acute_(medicine)" title="Acute (medicine)">\n        acute\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Burn" title="Burn">\n        burns\n       </a>\n       hospital for children, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Shriners_Hospitals_for_Children" title="Shriners Hospitals for Children">\n        Shriners Burns Hospital at Galveston\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-galvestondailynews.com_143-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-galvestondailynews.com-143">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Galveston hospital is one of only four in the chain of 22\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-profit" title="Non-profit">\n        non-profit\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Arabic_Order_of_the_Nobles_of_the_Mystic_Shrine" title="Ancient Arabic Order of the Nobles of the Mystic Shrine">\n        Shriners\n       </a>\n       hospitals, that provides acute burns care.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">\n        <a href="#cite_note-144">\n         [144]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Although the Galveston Hospital was damaged by Hurricane Ike, the Shriners national convention held in July 2009 voted to repair and reopen the hospital.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-galvestondailynews.com_143-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-galvestondailynews.com-143">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">\n        <a href="#cite_note-145">\n         [145]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fire_department">\n        Fire department\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Fire department">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Galveston Fire Department provides\n       <a href="/wiki/Fire_protection" title="Fire protection">\n        fire protection\n       </a>\n       services through six fire stations and 17 pieces of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fire_apparatus" title="Fire apparatus">\n        apparatus\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">\n        <a href="#cite_note-146">\n         [146]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130204034639/http://www.galvestonpolice.net/official/" rel="nofollow">\n        Galveston Police Department\n       </a>\n       has provided the city\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Police" title="Police">\n        police protection\n       </a>\n       for more than 165 years. Over 170 authorized officers serve in three divisions.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Library">\n        Library\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Library">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rosenberg_Library2008.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="558" data-file-width="1725" height="71" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Rosenberg_Library2008.jpg/220px-Rosenberg_Library2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Rosenberg_Library2008.jpg/330px-Rosenberg_Library2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Rosenberg_Library2008.jpg/440px-Rosenberg_Library2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rosenberg_Library2008.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Rosenberg Library\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The city is served by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rosenberg_Library" title="Rosenberg Library">\n        Rosenberg Library\n       </a>\n       , successor to the Galveston Mercantile Library, which was founded in 1871. It is the oldest public library in the State of Texas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rosenberg_147-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rosenberg-147">\n         [147]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">\n        <a href="#cite_note-148">\n         [148]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The library also serves as headquarters of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galveston_County_Library_System" title="Galveston County Library System">\n        Galveston County Library System\n       </a>\n       , and its librarian also functions as the Galveston County Librarian.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">\n        <a href="#cite_note-149">\n         [149]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Courts">\n        Courts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Courts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Galveston Division of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Southern_District_of_Texas" title="United States District Court for the Southern District of Texas">\n        United States District Court for the Southern District of Texas\n       </a>\n       , the first federal court in Texas, is based in Galveston and has jurisdiction over the counties of Galveston,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazoria_County" title="Brazoria County">\n        Brazoria\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Chambers_County,_Texas" title="Chambers County, Texas">\n        Chambers\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matagorda_County" title="Matagorda County">\n        Matagorda\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">\n        <a href="#cite_note-150">\n         [150]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is housed in the United States Post Office, Customs House and Court House federal building in downtown Galveston.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">\n        <a href="#cite_note-151">\n         [151]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">\n        United States Postal Service\n       </a>\n       operates several post offices in Galveston, including the Galveston Main Post Office and the Bob Lyons Post Office Station.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">\n        <a href="#cite_note-152">\n         [152]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">\n        <a href="#cite_note-153">\n         [153]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition the post office has a contract postal unit at the Medical Branch Unit on the campus of the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_Medical_Branch" title="University of Texas Medical Branch">\n        University of Texas Medical Branch\n       </a>\n       and the West Galveston\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service#Types_of_postal_facilities" title="United States Postal Service">\n        Contract Postal Unit\n       </a>\n       , located on the west end of Galveston Island in the beachside community of\n       <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Beach,_Texas" title="Jamaica Beach, Texas">\n        Jamaica Beach\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">\n        Transportation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Transportation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scholes_Field_Terminal,_Galveston.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1293" data-file-width="2566" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Scholes_Field_Terminal%2C_Galveston.jpg/220px-Scholes_Field_Terminal%2C_Galveston.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Scholes_Field_Terminal%2C_Galveston.jpg/330px-Scholes_Field_Terminal%2C_Galveston.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Scholes_Field_Terminal%2C_Galveston.jpg/440px-Scholes_Field_Terminal%2C_Galveston.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scholes_Field_Terminal,_Galveston.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Scholes_International_Airport_at_Galveston" title="Scholes International Airport at Galveston">\n          Scholes International Airport at Galveston\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air">\n        Air\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Air">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Scholes_International_Airport_at_Galveston" title="Scholes International Airport at Galveston">\n        Scholes International Airport at Galveston\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">\n        IATA\n       </a>\n       :\n       <b>\n        GLS\n       </b>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">\n        ICAO\n       </a>\n       :\n       <b>\n        KGLS\n       </b>\n       ) is a two-runway airport in Galveston; the airport is primarily used for general aviation, offshore energy transportation, and some limited military operations. The nearest commercial airline service for the city is operated out of Houston through\n       <a href="/wiki/William_P._Hobby_Airport" title="William P. Hobby Airport">\n        William P. Hobby Airport\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Bush_Intercontinental_Airport" title="George Bush Intercontinental Airport">\n        George Bush Intercontinental Airport\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_Medical_Branch" title="University of Texas Medical Branch">\n        University of Texas Medical Branch\n       </a>\n       has two heliports, one for Ewing Hall and one for its emergency room.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Railroad">\n        Railroad\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Railroad">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Railroad" title="Galveston Railroad">\n        Galveston Railway\n       </a>\n       , originally established and named in 1854 as the Galveston Wharf and Cotton Press Company, is a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_III_railroad" title="Class III railroad">\n        Class III\n       </a>\n       terminal switching railroad that primarily serves the transportation of cargo to and from the Port of Galveston. The railway operates 32 miles (51\xc2\xa0km) of yard track at Galveston, over a 50-acre (200,000\xc2\xa0m\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) facility.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">\n        <a href="#cite_note-154">\n         [154]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Island_Transit_(Texas)" title="Island Transit (Texas)">\n        Island Transit\n       </a>\n       , which operates the\n       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Island_Trolley" title="Galveston Island Trolley">\n        Galveston Island Trolley\n       </a>\n       manages the city\'s public transportation services. Intercity bus service to Galveston was previously operated by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kerrville_Bus" title="Kerrville Bus">\n        Kerrville Bus\n       </a>\n       Company; following the company\'s acquisition by Coach USA, service was operated by\n       <a href="/wiki/Megabus_(North_America)" title="Megabus (North America)">\n        Megabus\n       </a>\n       . All regular intercity bus service has been discontinued.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Galveston is served by\n       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">\n        Amtrak\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Texas_Eagle" title="Texas Eagle">\n         Texas Eagle\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       via connecting bus service at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Longview_(Amtrak_station)" title="Longview (Amtrak station)">\n        Longview, Texas\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">\n        Roads\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Roads">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_45" title="Interstate 45">\n        Interstate 45\n       </a>\n       has a southern terminus in Galveston and serves as a main artery to Galveston from mainland Galveston County and\n       <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">\n        Houston\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Farm_to_Market_Road_3005" title="Farm to Market Road 3005">\n        Farm to Market Road 3005\n       </a>\n       (locally called\n       <a href="/wiki/Seawall_Boulevard" title="Seawall Boulevard">\n        Seawall Boulevard\n       </a>\n       ) connects Galveston to\n       <a href="/wiki/Brazoria_County,_Texas" title="Brazoria County, Texas">\n        Brazoria County\n       </a>\n       via the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Luis_Pass-Vacek_Toll_Bridge" title="San Luis Pass-Vacek Toll Bridge">\n        San Luis Pass-Vacek Toll Bridge\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_State_Highway_87" title="Texas State Highway 87">\n        State Highway 87\n       </a>\n       , known locally as Broadway Street, connects the island to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolivar_Peninsula" title="Bolivar Peninsula">\n        Bolivar Peninsula\n       </a>\n       via the Bolivar Ferry. A project to construct the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bolivar_Bridge" title="Bolivar Bridge">\n        proposed Bolivar Bridge\n       </a>\n       to link Galveston to Bolivar Peninsula was cancelled in 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">\n        <a href="#cite_note-155">\n         [155]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">\n        Notable people\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Notable people">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jack_Johnson1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="508" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Jack_Johnson1.jpg/125px-Jack_Johnson1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Jack_Johnson1.jpg/188px-Jack_Johnson1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Jack_Johnson1.jpg/250px-Jack_Johnson1.jpg 2x" width="125"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jack_Johnson1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         World heavyweight boxer\n         <a href="/wiki/Jack_Johnson_(boxer)" title="Jack Johnson (boxer)">\n          Jack Johnson\n         </a>\n         , nicknamed the "Galveston Giant"\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Galveston has been home to many important figures in Texas and U.S. history. During the island\'s earliest history it became the domain of\n       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Lafitte" title="Jean Lafitte">\n        Jean Lafitte\n       </a>\n       , the famed\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pirate" title="Pirate">\n        pirate\n       </a>\n       and American hero of the\n       <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">\n        War of 1812\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HTOLAFITTE_8-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HTOLAFITTE-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richard_Bache_Jr._(Texas_politician)" title="Richard Bache Jr. (Texas politician)">\n        Richard Bache, Jr.\n       </a>\n       who represented Galveston in the Senate of the Second Texas Legislature in 1847 and assisted in drawing up the Constitution of 1845. He was also the grandson of\n       <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">\n        Benjamin Franklin\n       </a>\n       , one of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Founding_Fathers_of_the_United_States" title="Founding Fathers of the United States">\n        Founding Fathers\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       of America and\n       <a href="/wiki/Deborah_Read" title="Deborah Read">\n        Deborah Read\n       </a>\n       . In 1886, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American">\n        African-American\n       </a>\n       Galveston civil rights leader\n       <a href="/wiki/Norris_Wright_Cuney" title="Norris Wright Cuney">\n        Norris Wright Cuney\n       </a>\n       rose to become the head of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texas_Republican_Party" title="Texas Republican Party">\n        Texas Republican Party\n       </a>\n       and one of the most important\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_South" title="American South">\n        Southern\n       </a>\n       black leaders of the century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">\n        <a href="#cite_note-156">\n         [156]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Noted portrait and landscape artist\n       <a href="/wiki/Verner_Moore_White" title="Verner Moore White">\n        Verner Moore White\n       </a>\n       moved from Galveston the day before the 1900 hurricane. While he survived, his studio and much of his portfolio were destroyed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">\n        <a href="#cite_note-157">\n         [157]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A survivor of the hurricane was the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">\n        Hollywood\n       </a>\n       director\n       <a href="/wiki/King_Vidor" title="King Vidor">\n        King Vidor\n       </a>\n       , who made his directing debut in 1913 with the film\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_in_Galveston" title="Hurricane in Galveston">\n         Hurricane in Galveston\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">\n        <a href="#cite_note-158">\n         [158]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Later\n       <a href="/wiki/Jack_Johnson_(boxer)" title="Jack Johnson (boxer)">\n        Jack Johnson\n       </a>\n       , nicknamed the \xe2\x80\x9cGalveston Giant\xe2\x80\x9d, became the first black world heavyweight boxing champion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">\n        <a href="#cite_note-159">\n         [159]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the first half of the 20th century,\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Lewis_Moody_Jr." title="William Lewis Moody Jr.">\n        William L. Moody Jr.\n       </a>\n       established a business empire, which includes\n       <a href="/wiki/American_National_Insurance_Company" title="American National Insurance Company">\n        American National Insurance Company\n       </a>\n       , a major national insurer, and founded the\n       <a href="/wiki/Moody_Foundation" title="Moody Foundation">\n        Moody Foundation\n       </a>\n       , one of the largest charitable organizations in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">\n        <a href="#cite_note-160">\n         [160]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Sam_Maceo" title="Sam Maceo">\n        Sam Maceo\n       </a>\n       , a nationally known\n       <a href="/wiki/Organized_crime" title="Organized crime">\n        organized crime\n       </a>\n       boss, with the help of his family, was largely responsible for making Galveston a major U.S. tourist destination from the 1920s to the 1940s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hotgalv_38-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hotgalv-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=John_H._Murphy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="John H. Murphy (page does not exist)">\n        John H. Murphy\n       </a>\n       , a Texas newspaperman for seventy-four years, was the longtime executive vice president of the Texas Daily Newspaper Association.\n       <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Corrigan" title="Douglas Corrigan">\n        Douglas Corrigan\n       </a>\n       became one of the early transatlantic aviators, and was given the nickname "Wrong Way" for claiming to have mistakenly made the ocean crossing after being refused permission to make the flight.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">\n        <a href="#cite_note-161">\n         [161]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Grammy-award-winning singer-songwriter\n       <a href="/wiki/Barry_White" title="Barry White">\n        Barry White\n       </a>\n       was born on the island and later moved to Los Angeles.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/George_P._Mitchell" title="George P. Mitchell">\n        George P. Mitchell\n       </a>\n       , pioneer of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydraulic_fracturing" title="Hydraulic fracturing">\n        hydraulic fracturing\n       </a>\n       technology and developer of\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Woodlands,_Texas" title="The Woodlands, Texas">\n        The Woodlands, Texas\n       </a>\n       , was born and raised in Galveston.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Anita_Martini" title="Anita Martini">\n        Anita Martini\n       </a>\n       , pioneering female sports journalist who was the first woman allowed in a major league locker room for a post-game press conference, was born in Galveston.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       More recently\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tilman_J._Fertitta" title="Tilman J. Fertitta">\n        Tilman J. Fertitta\n       </a>\n       , part of the Maceo bloodline, established the Landry\'s Restaurants corporation, which owns numerous restaurants and entertainment venues in Texas and Nevada.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">\n        <a href="#cite_note-162">\n         [162]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Kay_Bailey_Hutchison" title="Kay Bailey Hutchison">\n        Kay Bailey Hutchison\n       </a>\n       was the senior\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">\n        senator\n       </a>\n       from Texas and the first female Texas senator.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">\n        <a href="#cite_note-163">\n         [163]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gilbert_Pena" title="Gilbert Pena">\n        Gilbert Pena\n       </a>\n       , incoming 2015 Republican member of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_House_of_Representatives" title="Texas House of Representatives">\n        Texas House of Representatives\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_Texas" title="Pasadena, Texas">\n        Pasadena\n       </a>\n       , was born in Galveston in 1949 and lived there in early childhood.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">\n        <a href="#cite_note-164">\n         [164]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Pollard" title="Jonathan Pollard">\n        Jonathan Pollard\n       </a>\n       , who spied for\n       <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">\n        Israel\n       </a>\n       and was convicted in the US and sentenced to life in jail, was born in Galveston.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trahair2004_165-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Trahair2004-165">\n         [165]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The film and television actor\n       <a href="/wiki/Lee_Patterson" title="Lee Patterson">\n        Lee Patterson\n       </a>\n       , a native of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vancouver,_British_Columbia" title="Vancouver, British Columbia">\n        Vancouver, British Columbia\n       </a>\n       , lived in Galveston and died there in 2007.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other notable people include\n       <a href="/wiki/Matt_Carpenter_(baseball)" title="Matt Carpenter (baseball)">\n        Matt Carpenter\n       </a>\n       , second baseman for the\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">\n        St. Louis Cardinals\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">\n        <a href="#cite_note-166">\n         [166]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mike_Evans_(wide_receiver)" title="Mike Evans (wide receiver)">\n        Mike Evans\n       </a>\n       , wide receiver for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Buccaneers" title="Tampa Bay Buccaneers">\n        Tampa Bay Buccaneers\n       </a>\n       , 1998\n       <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">\n        Heisman Trophy\n       </a>\n       runner-up and pro quarterback\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bishop_(gridiron_football)" title="Michael Bishop (gridiron football)">\n        Michael Bishop\n       </a>\n       , comedian\n       <a href="/wiki/Bill_Engvall" title="Bill Engvall">\n        Bill Engvall\n       </a>\n       , actress\n       <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Helmond" title="Katherine Helmond">\n        Katherine Helmond\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tina_Knowles" title="Tina Knowles">\n        Tina Knowles\n       </a>\n       , fashion designer and creator of\n       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Der%C3%A9on" title="House of Der\xc3\xa9on">\n        House of Der\xc3\xa9on\n       </a>\n       , mother of\n       <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyonc\xc3\xa9">\n        Beyonc\xc3\xa9\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Solange" title="Solange">\n        Solange\n       </a>\n       . Grammy award-winning R&amp;B and Jazz legend\n       <a href="/wiki/Esther_Phillips" title="Esther Phillips">\n        Esther Phillips\n       </a>\n       was born in Galveston in 1935.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Galveston_in_media_and_literature">\n        Galveston in media and literature\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galveston,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Galveston in media and literature">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        "\n        <a href="/wiki/Galveston_(song)" title="Galveston (song)">\n         Galveston\n        </a>\n        " is the name of a popular song written by\n        <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Webb" title="Jimmy Webb">\n         Jimmy Webb\n        </a>\n        and sung by\n        <a href="/wiki/Glen_Campbell" title="Glen Campbell">\n         Glen Campbell\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Sheldon_Cooper" title="Sheldon Cooper">\n         Sheldon Cooper\n        </a>\n        , one of the main characters from the\n        <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">\n         CBS\n        </a>\n        <a href="/wiki/Sitcom" title="Sitcom">\n         sitcom\n        </a>\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/The_Big_Bang_Theory" title="The Big Bang Theory">\n          The Big Bang Theory\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        , grew up in Galveston. Galveston will be the setting for the upcoming\n        <a href="/wiki/Spin-off_(media)" title="Spin-off (media)">\n         spin-off\n        </a>\n        series\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Young_Sheldon" title="Young Sheldon">\n          Young Sheldon\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        , dealing with the character\'s life as a child.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The theater film,\n        <i>\n         The Man from Galveston\n        </i>\n        (1963), was the original\n        <a href="/wiki/Television_pilot" title="Television pilot">\n         pilot episode\n        </a>\n        of the proposed\n        <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">\n         NBC\n        </a>\n        <a href="/wiki/Western_(genre)" title="Western (genre)">\n         western\n        </a>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Television_series" title="Television series">\n         television series\n        </a>\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Temple_Houston_(TV_series)" title="Temple Houston (TV series)">\n          Temple Houston\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        , with\n        <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Hunter" title="Jeffrey Hunter">\n         Jeffrey Hunter\n        </a>\n        cast as\n        <a href="/wiki/Temple_Lea_Houston" title="Temple Lea Houston">\n         Temple Lea Houston\n        </a>\n        , a lawyer and the youngest son of the legendary\n        <a href="/wiki/Sam_Houston" title="Sam Houston">\n         Sam Houston\n        </a>\n        . For a time the real Temple Houston was the county attorney of\n        <a href="/wiki/Brazoria_County,_Texas" title="Brazoria County, Texas">\n         Brazoria County\n        </a>\n        , Texas. The\n        <i>\n         Temple Houston\n        </i>\n        series lasted for only twenty-six episodes in the 1963-1964 television season.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">\n         <a href="#cite_note-167">\n          [167]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Donald_Barthelme" title="Donald Barthelme">\n         Donald Barthelme\n        </a>\n        \'s 1974\n        <a href="/wiki/Short_story" title="Short story">\n         short story\n        </a>\n        "I bought a little city" is about an unnamed man who invests his fortune in buying Galveston, only to sell it thereafter.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">\n         <a href="#cite_note-168">\n          [168]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Galveston is the setting of\n        <a href="/wiki/Sean_Stewart" title="Sean Stewart">\n         Sean Stewart\n        </a>\n        \'s 2000 fantasy novel\n        <i>\n         Galveston,\n        </i>\n        in which a Flood of Magic takes over the island city, resulting in strange and carnivalesque adventures. It tied in 2001 with\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Declare" title="Declare">\n          Declare\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        , by\n        <a href="/wiki/Tim_Powers" title="Tim Powers">\n         Tim Powers\n        </a>\n        , for the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Fantasy_Award_for_Best_Novel" title="World Fantasy Award for Best Novel">\n         World Fantasy Award for Best Novel\n        </a>\n        . It also won the 2001\n        <a href="/wiki/Sunburst_Award" title="Sunburst Award">\n         Sunburst Award\n        </a>\n        and was a preliminary nominee for the\n        <a href="/wiki/Nebula_Award_for_Best_Novel" title="Nebula Award for Best Novel">\n         Nebula Award for Best Novel\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         The Drowning House\n        </i>\n        , a novel by Elizabeth Black (2013), is an exploration of the island of Galveston, Texas, and the intertwined histories of two families who reside there.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">\n         <a href="#cite_note-169">\n          [169]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Stephenie Meyer has mentioned Galveston island in her third book of the Twilight series, Eclipse.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         Galveston\n        </i>\n        (2010) is the first novel by\n        <a href="/wiki/Nic_Pizzolatto" title="Nic Pizzolatto">\n         Nic Pizzolatto\n        </a>\n        , the creator of the\n        <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">\n         HBO\n        </a>\n        series\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/True_Detective_(TV_series)" title="True Detective (TV series)">\n         <i>\n          True Detective\n         </i>\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/The_Jinx_(miniseries)" title="The Jinx (miniseries)">\n          The Jinx\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        (2015), an\n        <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">\n         HBO\n        </a>\n        miniseries, features Galveston as home to one of\n        <a href="/wiki/Robert_Durst" title="Robert Durst">\n         Robert Durst\n        </a>\n        \'s murders which took place in 2001.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities">\n        Sister cities\n       </span>\n
